  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dbb30d40-cf63-465b-a10c-62efc0106296'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

            var lessLink = e.next();

        });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6213743978297167923">When struggling riverboat captain Abner Marsh receives an offer of partnership from a wealthy aristocrat, he suspects something’s amiss. But when he meets the hauntingly pale, steely-eyed Joshua York, he is certain. For York doesn’t care that the icy winter of 1857 has wiped out all but one of Marsh’s dilapidated fleet. Nor does he care that he won’t earn back his investme</span>
  <span id="freeText6213743978297167923" style="display:none">When struggling riverboat captain Abner Marsh receives an offer of partnership from a wealthy aristocrat, he suspects something’s amiss. But when he meets the hauntingly pale, steely-eyed Joshua York, he is certain. For York doesn’t care that the icy winter of 1857 has wiped out all but one of Marsh’s dilapidated fleet. Nor does he care that he won’t earn back his investment in a decade. York has his own reasons for wanting to traverse the powerful Mississippi. And they are to be none of Marsh’s concern—no matter how bizarre, arbitrary, or capricious his actions may prove. <br /><br />Marsh meant to turn down York’s offer. It was too full of secrets that spelled danger. But the promise of both gold and a grand new boat that could make history crushed his resolve—coupled with the terrible force of York’s mesmerizing gaze. Not until the maiden voyage of his new sidewheeler Fevre Dream would Marsh realize he had joined a mission both more sinister, and perhaps more noble, than his most fantastic nightmare...and mankind’s most impossible dream. <br /><br />Here is the spellbinding tale of a vampire’s quest to unite his race with humanity, of a garrulous riverman’s dream of immortality, and of the undying legends of the steamboat era and a majestic, ancient river.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6213743978297167923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5710178944261574265"><b>Fevre Dream، c1982, George R.R. Martin</b><br/><br/>Fevre Dream is a 1982 vampire novel written by American author George R. R. Martin. It is set on the antebellum Mississippi River, beginning in 1857, and has been described by critics and Martin himself as "Bram Stoker meets Mark Twain". <br/><br/>Abner Marsh, a remarkably unattractive but highly skilled Mississippi River steamboat captain, is grappling with a financial crisis in 1857 when he is contacted by Joshua York, a rich, soft-spoken gentleman. <br/><br/>تاریخ نخستین خوا</span>
  <span id="freeText5710178944261574265" style="display:none"><b>Fevre Dream، c1982, George R.R. Martin</b><br /><br />Fevre Dream is a 1982 vampire novel written by American author George R. R. Martin. It is set on the antebellum Mississippi River, beginning in 1857, and has been described by critics and Martin himself as "Bram Stoker meets Mark Twain". <br /><br />Abner Marsh, a remarkably unattractive but highly skilled Mississippi River steamboat captain, is grappling with a financial crisis in 1857 when he is contacted by Joshua York, a rich, soft-spoken gentleman. <br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه جولای سال 2014میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: رویای تب‌ آلود؛ نویسنده: جورج آر.آر. مارتین؛ مترجم: میلاد فشتمی؛ تهران، بهنام، 1392؛ در 519ص؛ شابک 9789645668875؛ موضوع: داستانهای ترسناک از نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 20م<br /><br />،داستان این رمان در روزهای نخست سال 1857میلادی در امتداد رود می.سی.سی.پی رخ میدهد؛ بسیاری این رمان را یکی از سه رمان خون آشامی برتر تاریخ نامیده اند؛ رمان نخستین بار در جهان به سال 1982میلادی، توسط انتشارات «پوسیدون» به چاپ رسید<br /><br />نقل از متن: «رستوران با آن چلچراغ‌های باشکوه، مبلمان برنجی، رومیزی‌های کتان و ظروف چینی و کریستال؛ تقریباً به بزرگی و زیبایی سالن اصلی یک کشتی بخار بود؛ در طول روز احتمالاً تمام میزها پر از مشتری بودند، ولی اکنون سالن خالی، و بیشتر چراغ‌ها خاموش بودند؛ مارش با خود فکر کرد، که قرار ملاقات در نیمه‌ شب حداقل این خوبی را دارد، که دیگر نیازی نیست به تسلیت‌ها و همدردی‌های ملوانان دیگر گوش کند؛ در نزدیکی درِ آشپزخانه، دو کارگر سیاه‌پوست آرام مشغول گفتگو بودند؛ «مارش» بی‌توجه از کنارشان گذشت، و به سمت انتهای سالن ـ جاییکه غریبه‌ ای خوشپوش، تنها مشغول غذا خوردن بود ـ حرکت کرد؛ غریبه احتمالاً صدای پایش را شنیده بود، ولی بدون اینکه سرش را بلند کند، همچنان به خوردن سوپ لاک‌پشت ادامه می‌داد؛ کت بلند مشکی‌ اش، به وضوح نشان می‌داد، که ملوان نیست؛ احتمالاً از اهالی شرق بود، و یا حتی یک خارجی. هیکل درشتی داشت، اما به تنومندی «مارش» نبود؛ در همان حالت نشسته هم، به نظر می‌رسید، که قدبلند باشد، با این حال مطمئناً از «مارش» کوتاه‌تر بود.»؛ پایان نقل...؛ <br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 06/08/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1621044327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1621044327" />
    <a title="Reading Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46088881-reading-corner"><img alt="Reading Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440473163p2/46088881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1621044327?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Corner" href="/user/show/46088881-reading-corner">Reading Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407247298" href="/book/show/21532730-fevre-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1621044327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15481345915006892596"><i>Fevre Dream</i> uses a blend of historical fiction and mythology to create an exciting vampire story that deviates from the others.The protagonist, Abner Marsh,a renowned steamboat captain is approached by Joshua York who desires Marsh's help in creating the perfect steamboat.Of course Marsh agrees as his goal is to outrace the biggest and best steamboats on the river.However, his goal is stunted as York has plans of his which intertwine with his aims for his people, as he is a vampire.<br/><br/>The plot is r</span>
  <span id="freeText15481345915006892596" style="display:none"><i>Fevre Dream</i> uses a blend of historical fiction and mythology to create an exciting vampire story that deviates from the others.The protagonist, Abner Marsh,a renowned steamboat captain is approached by Joshua York who desires Marsh's help in creating the perfect steamboat.Of course Marsh agrees as his goal is to outrace the biggest and best steamboats on the river.However, his goal is stunted as York has plans of his which intertwine with his aims for his people, as he is a vampire.<br /><br />The plot is riveting as I found myself asking a lot of questions and anticipating what was going to happen next.The setting was fascinating as the story mainly takes place on the steamboat and is where the historical element comes into the play.Parts of the novel were a bit weak where the plans were just incredibly dumb and obviously not going to work.Also, towards the end this got a bit annoying as their mistakes just became repetitive.<br /><br />Most of the characters are well written,especially Marsh who is humorous and entertaining whereas York is intriguing and mysterious.The villain was a little overdone as he lacked cause for doing things and quickly became predictable.<br /><br />As a whole the story is gripping and the writing is good.I haven't read many vampire novels but this one is definitely different to what I've watched and read.<i>Fevre Dream</i> is definitely worth checking out if you're a fan of horror or paranormal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15481345915006892596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_826633505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826633505" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826633505?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=darkness-horror-gothic">darkness-horror-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=3-star-reads">3-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826633505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2965454168408947412">Abner March looks strangely like George R.R Martin. They are both overweight men. They both have long beards and wear sea captain’s hats. I’m not sure who came first. Perhaps Martin modelled the character off of his own appearance or perhaps he liked his creation so much that he was compelled to try the style himself. It’s a little bit weird really, though the book is still quite good even if the protagonist is somewhat laughable in his resemblance of his creator.<br/><br/>This is the French cover:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450184907i/17390821.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>They ju</span>
  <span id="freeText2965454168408947412" style="display:none">Abner March looks strangely like George R.R Martin. They are both overweight men. They both have long beards and wear sea captain’s hats. I’m not sure who came first. Perhaps Martin modelled the character off of his own appearance or perhaps he liked his creation so much that he was compelled to try the style himself. It’s a little bit weird really, though the book is still quite good even if the protagonist is somewhat laughable in his resemblance of his creator.<br><br>This is the French cover:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450184907i/17390821.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They just look very similar. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450185234i/17390854._SX540_.png" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> A tub full of blood </b><br><br> <s> George R.R Martin </s> Abner Marsh is a steamboat captain and he, quite naturally, longs for a majestic steamer that will outpace all others. But, he has no money. Conversely, Joshua York is a very, very, rich man who needs a boat to help him conduct his nocturnal lifestyle. He lacks the skills of the trade, so the two pair up. They provide the other with what he lacks though creating a mutually beneficial friendship. Abner gets his boat and Joshua gets his hideout; they both win. <br><br>Well, not entirely because Joshua has a dark past. His is a vampire. I think he is characterised superbly in this; he is strong and intense, but at the same time he is open and capable. With his dark powers he could carry out great evil, if he so chose, but he has transcended the limitations of his body and become a morally superior being in the process. He has devised a way to satisfy his thirst without harming anyone. He is a good vampire rather than the demonic blood sucking maniacs that infest this world. And when these said maniacs begin to sniff around Abner’s boat, the two friends have their dreams crushed. So much for a lovely steamboat adventure, the very walls turn red in the action. <br><br><b> A pointless bad guy</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450184355i/17390785._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Now here comes the book’s massive hindrance. Its antagonist, Damien Julien, is an ancient vampire and his ethos is in direct contrast to Joshua’s. He loves blood and he doesn’t care who he tears open to get it. The man’s practically a god. He’s top of the food chain. He can have what he wants when he wants it. He is a typical vampire; he is dark and brooding, but he is also fundamentally flawed. He has no reason to exist. As he himself admits, he has no reason for anything. He just does it because he can. I think for him to be a more effective and dramatic opponent of Joshua’s, he needed to have a dark motive or a hidden evil that drove him. At the moment he has no reason to do anything. <br><br>I found him to be completely disappointing. He had no drive or passion even to do evil. He just does it. The character could have been so much more than he was. I’d rather he was just a basic evil architype than this. It would have been better if he just wanted to rule the world or something. At least that way, he would have a reason to get out of bed at night (see what I did there!) Joshua and Abner were well rounded characters whose actions actually had a reason. They saved the book in my estimation even if the final conflicts were a little bit flat. It should have been a battle of polar opposites. <br><br><b> A good three stars </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2965454168408947412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630120830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8637338709295631872">The year is 1982 and while there have been a ton of traditional vampire novels floating about, the big twist in the vampire industry hasn't quite come about yet with Interview... or has it? Enter Fevre Dream, taking this our darkest mirror to our humanity and turning him into something tragic and noble and throwing him into a Mark Twain novel.<br/><br/>What? Mark Twain? Oh yeah, steamboats, 1857, we've got 15 mile an hour races and chases and deeply disturbing looks at what makes men monsters and what mak</span>
  <span id="freeText8637338709295631872" style="display:none">The year is 1982 and while there have been a ton of traditional vampire novels floating about, the big twist in the vampire industry hasn't quite come about yet with Interview... or has it? Enter Fevre Dream, taking this our darkest mirror to our humanity and turning him into something tragic and noble and throwing him into a Mark Twain novel.<br /><br />What? Mark Twain? Oh yeah, steamboats, 1857, we've got 15 mile an hour races and chases and deeply disturbing looks at what makes men monsters and what makes monsters into men. Hate being a cow or a slave? Hate being a slave to your baser instincts, and have you decided never to simply give into them, unlike so many others? How heroic. :) Of course, this came out a good deal before our current glut and, at least to me, it marks a sudden and fantastic development in the whole field.<br /><br />Sure, we might have had some sympathy for the original Dracula, just as we have sympathy for the Devil, but the heroes were much more often outside of the curse. And up till now, Vampires were still just the expression of truly base humanity, not worth much redeeming. <br /><br />So this human aspect is truly excellent in the tale, but don't let me downplay the real gem here: steamboats. Total immersion in the world. Totally cool. I never guessed that chugging along at 8 miles per hour could be so exciting! But of course, that's all due to a master storyteller. :) GRRM has been around for a long, long time, practicing a very fine craft. We really shouldn't forget that. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8637338709295631872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_203506600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203506600" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203506600?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203506600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12609999757819548310">I almost gave up vampire fiction in the wake of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61034231' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twilight</a>. Stephenie Meyer wrote the novel to pander to a certain demographic without any familiarity or respect for classic vampire fiction of the past century. Unfortunately, the Twilight saga is very commercially successful and spawned many imitators, lame wishy washy vampire books, and the entire “paranormal romance” subgenre (￢_￢;). I don't know if good "proper" vampire fiction is still being written these days, but the great ones are still aro</span>
  <span id="freeText12609999757819548310" style="display:none">I almost gave up vampire fiction in the wake of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61034231" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>. Stephenie Meyer wrote the novel to pander to a certain demographic without any familiarity or respect for classic vampire fiction of the past century. Unfortunately, the Twilight saga is very commercially successful and spawned many imitators, lame wishy washy vampire books, and the entire “paranormal romance” subgenre (￢_￢;). I don't know if good "proper" vampire fiction is still being written these days, but the great ones are still around and are well worth checking out if you are a horror fan. From Bram Stoker’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17245.Dracula" title="Dracula by Bram Stoker" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dracula</a> to King’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11590._Salem_s_Lot" title="'Salem's Lot by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> Salem’s Lot</a>, Anne Rice’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_" title="Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener"> Interview with the Vampire</a>, Richard Matheson's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14064.I_Am_Legend" title="I Am Legend by Richard Matheson" rel="nofollow noopener"> I Am Legend</a> and several others. This book, <i>Fevre Dream</i> is also one of the greats.<br> <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin" title="George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener"> George R.R. Martin</a> is, of course, best known for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener"> Game of Thrones</a> (“A Song of Ice and Fire” series) but prior to that runaway success he has written several excellent sci-fi stories and novels. <i>Fevre Dream</i> was published in 1982, I read it at some point in the 80s and it has stayed with me to this day. The story is set in 1857 when steamboats dominated trade on the Mississippi River. Captain Abner Marsh forms a partnership with a mysterious stranger named Joshua York whose offer to build the captain’s dream boat to co-own as a business partner. It transpires that York is a vampire who is also something of a visionary or even messiah among his kind. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477842073i/20999883._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="575" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>His life mission is to redeem the vampire rate and bring about peaceful co-existence with mankind, using a steamboat as his long-distance transportation of choice to facilitate his plans. Not an easy task because humans provide the basic sustenance for vampires, and are generally referred to as “cattle” among them. Worse still there is a master vampire called Damon Julian who lives on a plantation with his human and vampire underlings in New Orleans. Julian is something of a traditionalist and views vampires as the master race and humans as cattle. When the two mega vamps meet a very bloody struggle for supremacy begins. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477842464i/20999936._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="309" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>All this and lots of steamboating!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477842073i/20999884.jpg" width="400" height="267" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Fevre Dream</i> is a gripping and thrilling read, especially in the second half of the book where the pages just fly by. The type of vampirism presented here is what I call “sci-fi vampires”, similar to Octavia Butler’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60925.Fledgling" title="Fledgling by Octavia E. Butler" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fledgling</a> and Richard Matheson’s classic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14064.I_Am_Legend" title="I Am Legend by Richard Matheson" rel="nofollow noopener"> I Am Legend</a>. Vampires in this book are simply a different species from humans, it is not possible to convert from one race to the other; garlic, crucifix, holy water etc. have no effect on them. Sunlight is still deadly to them, though.<br><br>Besides being a first race horror thriller <i>Fevre Dream</i> also partly a slave narrative, where the slaves are treated cruelly by both humans and vampires. The relations between human and the vampire race are also something of an allegory for slavery and exploitation. The main characters are very well developed, vivid and unforgettable. Interestingly both the good and the evil vampire has a human sidekick to help out with the daytime practical affairs and business. Martin makes an interesting contrast between a friendly partnership and a master and servant relationship built upon deception and false promises.<br><br>The prose style is based on the point of view of the human sidekicks from the good and the evil side. As such it is written mostly in simple colloquial style. The unlikely friendship between Captain March and Joshua York is quite touching and forms the moral bedrock of the entire book. The climax is really quite spectacular and unforgettable.<br><br>If you are in the mood for some fast-paced horror and have not been put off vampire fiction by Twilight this book is highly recommended.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450184355i/17390785._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="551" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>_________________<br><br><b>Quotes:</b><br><i>“Cynthia embraced him by the alley, and gave him a lingering wet kiss. He thrashed and struggled but could not break free of her embrace. Her pale hands brushed the back of his neck, and long nails sharp and thin as razors slid across his veins. Her mouth and tongue swallowed his scream.”<br> <br>“The night is beautiful, and we can hope to find peace and nobility in its dark splendor as well. Too many men fear the dark unreasoningly.”<br> <br>“Within the hour I was out on the streets. I found an alley, waited. A young woman was the first to pass. Part of me admired her beauty; it burned in me like a flame. Another part simply hungered. I almost tore her head off, but at least it was over quickly. Afterward I wept.”<br> <br>“that roast you so enjoyed was once part of a living animal. Do you suppose that, if that beast could talk, he would consent to being eaten?”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12609999757819548310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_402237249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/402237249" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/594215-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543117893p2/594215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/402237249?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/594215-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer402237249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16853066090186944604">To enjoy this book, there are some things that I honestly believe that you must possess. <br/><br/>1. A love of steamboats, because <i>goddamn</i> does this book go on and on about steamboats. The main character, Abner Marsh, is a steamboat captain with an obsessive love of steamboats, and as is typical of Martin's writing when he gets Really Involved with something, every single tiny facet of the boat is described...sadly leaving the actually interesting parts, mainly those regarding the pasts of his vampire ch</span>
  <span id="freeText16853066090186944604" style="display:none">To enjoy this book, there are some things that I honestly believe that you must possess. <br /><br />1. A love of steamboats, because <i>goddamn</i> does this book go on and on about steamboats. The main character, Abner Marsh, is a steamboat captain with an obsessive love of steamboats, and as is typical of Martin's writing when he gets Really Involved with something, every single tiny facet of the boat is described...sadly leaving the actually interesting parts, mainly those regarding the pasts of his vampire characters, touched upon but lacking. Valerie in particular gets the short end of the stick, as all we learn of her is that she's very beautiful and, surprise surprise, in love with one of the other characters. Huzzah. Despite of course setting the framework for what could be a quite intriguing cast of characters, he leaves a lot of them really lacking and one-dimensional, which is especially a shame if you happen to read <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i> before this book and are aware of how much better he could have done. <br /><br />2. Absolutely no inkling of offense at the word "nigger". <i>Everyone</i> in this book, save for the vampires, uses that term to refer to their slaves. Yes, it's the 1870s, so there is a certain realism in it, but it gets trying around the tenth or so time that someone goes on a nonsensical tirade of nigger-this-nigger-that--and of course, all the people of color in this book speak like Civil-War Deep South Stereotypical Black People, with the full on 'Yessuh/Nossuh' and so many apostrophes that you almost start to get dizzy from how often your eyes go up and down over the page. <br /><br />3. Actually, no offense at racism whatsoever. It's used so often as an excuse to brutalize black people that if that kind of thing makes you upset, just...step back. (Blah blah historical realism yes we know, but if you're Really Offended at that kind of mindset...not a good plan to read this book.) <br /><br />4. Patience. It took me <i>far</i> too long to get through this book. The gaps between the remotely interesting bits that I blazed through were much too long, and even when I finally did reach the Big Climax of the Novel, it left me really underwhelmed; perhaps because at that point I no longer really cared about any of the characters or what happened because it had been so long since any characterization had actually taken place outside of 'here is the enemy' and 'here are the good guys'. <br /><br />At first, this book sounded like an interesting read from an author I honestly enjoy--I picked it up because there aren't that many English-language books to choose from, and I actually rather like vampire stories that refrain from romanticising the hell out of the vampire to the point that they're just Average People Who Happen to Have Inconvenient-At-Times Powers...but this was less about characters, and more an underdeveloped Moby Dick scenario with steamboats. So many steamboats. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16853066090186944604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1411191155" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1411191155" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1411191155?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553577938" href="/book/show/12894834-fevre-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=got-in-2015">got-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=sad">sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=serial-killer">serial-killer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1411191155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8682220523573840144"><br/><b>“Good and evil are silly lies, nonsense put forth to plague honest sensible men.” </b><br/><br/>Technology keeps improving but some parts of life and glory will be lost in the process.<br/><br/>Fevre Dream is a beautiful, multi-layered story that stands as a historical drama bordering fantasy and horror. It's more in line with Urban Fantasy because of the vampires that come out of the fog in our current world, the historical setting plays up on the atmosphere of the old steamboats and their glories, and - while not out</span>
  <span id="freeText8682220523573840144" style="display:none"><br /><b>“Good and evil are silly lies, nonsense put forth to plague honest sensible men.” </b><br /><br />Technology keeps improving but some parts of life and glory will be lost in the process.<br /><br />Fevre Dream is a beautiful, multi-layered story that stands as a historical drama bordering fantasy and horror. It's more in line with Urban Fantasy because of the vampires that come out of the fog in our current world, the historical setting plays up on the atmosphere of the old steamboats and their glories, and - while not outright horror - there are chills and quietly disturbing scenes delivered in atmospheric misery. A wonderful mixture of genres that refuses to be strictly defined.<br /><br />I fell in love with the hero of the book, Captain Abner Marsh, a man who lived for his life on the river. I can't say why he was so enamoring; maybe it was his enthusiasm and drive in life to live his dreams. He was suitably flawed, crass, crude, ill-tempered. His appearance was described often as awful and it was clear he'd long ago left aside any illusions of attracting people and living a life as a married man. Instead he married the river and never looked back. <br /><br />In an end of the year reading survey, one of the questions is to name the favorite characters I discovered in 2015. One of them was Augustus from Lonesome Dove, and one of them was Abner Marsh of Fevre Dream. <br /><br />The steamboats become characters of their own. I never thought much about them before, but this book brings to mind the joy that must have existed with them once upon a time. They were brought to a sort of life by the men who spent their lives building, dreaming, running, and racing these boats. <br /><br />George R.R. Martin's writing style charmed me in this haunting tale. The man has a way with words that is as captivating as the magic he reminisces. Slower, sedate pace proves not to be a problem because the words are so gorgeous, the characters rich, the story enchanting. <br /><br />This isn't the usual vampire tale - no sparkly vampires here, but really no actual vampires as we've known them before anyway. And that is okay, because it wouldn't make sense Martin would give us the typical, overdone fare. Some people only like the cruel, demented, soulless creatures that started with Dracula lore and legend, but this is a refreshing and non-romantic, realistic look at another sort. I enjoy three-dimensional creatures over flat paper creations, so Joshua York fits the bill ideally, but just in case we do also get an insane and twisted enemy for him to stand against and beside.<br /><br />The ending is sad but inevitable, leaving me with me with a depressed but contented feel. Bittersweet nostalgia and gripping wrap-up match the tone of the book. Abner starts as a man who has lost his world when his company dwindled, saw the chance to live again - and live he did, but as we all know good things don't last forever.<br /><br />You would think a book of this length being spent mainly on a boat would have boring lulls, but that wasn't the case at all. I was as entranced with the book as the men who rode these were by the river. There was a dreamy vibe felt when reading it; I could almost smell and picture those foggy nights and riding under that moon he described. Stunning stuff, the feeling comes back as I recall the story.<br /><br />Recommended as a different adventure into the mind of a fantasy legend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8682220523573840144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_86808219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86808219" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86808219?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781857983319" href="/book/show/757041.Fevre_Dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=wife-books">wife-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=must-read-in-2014">must-read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=ces-recommends">ces-recommends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86808219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13290358719252216483"><br/>Yet another interesting spin on the Vampire mythos, <i>Fevre Dream</i> is a delightfully atmospheric historical horror-drama. It skirts dangerously close to the boundary between Horror and Urban Fantasy, but it still manages to stir up some legitimate scares. This is George R.R. Martin, after all, and one or two of the more disturbing scenes will likely echo with you for an uncomfortable space of time.<br/><br/><i>That night he dreamt. In his dreams he was dark and graceful, elegant and predatory. It was always nig</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13290358719252216483" style="display:none"><br />Yet another interesting spin on the Vampire mythos, <i>Fevre Dream</i> is a delightfully atmospheric historical horror-drama. It skirts dangerously close to the boundary between Horror and Urban Fantasy, but it still manages to stir up some legitimate scares. This is George R.R. Martin, after all, and one or two of the more disturbing scenes will likely echo with you for an uncomfortable space of time.<br /><br /><i>That night he dreamt. In his dreams he was dark and graceful, elegant and predatory. It was always night in his dreams, and he roamed the streets of New Orleans beneath a full, pale moon.</i><br /><br />That said, it isn’t a scare-a-minute story this. There’s a <b>lot</b> of build up here. The characters are colourful and well presented, but there isn’t much in the sense of progression. You’ll find yourself more than a little frustrated when the protagonists fail to follow through on obvious solutions and when, a 100 pages or so later, the status quo is exactly the same. In fact, fully half the book consists of what can only be described as an impasse… or stalemate. <br /><br /><i>Through the dark he stalked them, gliding soundlessly over the brick sidewalks, hearing their frantic footsteps and their panting.</i><br /><br />Fortunately, this isn’t an oversight on the author’s part. The frustration Martin generates with his story is integral to the plot, but it does make for some uneasy reading. There are also some parallels drawn between slavery and the Vampire “culture” (for lack of a better word). If this doesn’t make sense, you need to read the book.<br /><br /><i>The night was his, and all the nights forever, and the red thirst was on him.</i><br /><br />The title of the book, which also happens to be the name of a Steam Boat featuring prominently in the story, is rather apt. The story has a feverish quality to it, as if everything is being filtered through your drug of choice. It’s good stuff, but it straddles a precarious line between Horror, History and Fantasy. I’m not sure whether this will appeal to everyone, but I will definitely recommend it.<br /><br />I read the <i>Fantasy Masterworks</i> edition.<br /><br /><i>When he woke from the dream, he was hot and fevered, and his sheets were wet.</i><br /><br /><br /><i>4 Stars</i><br /><i>Read as part of the must-read agreement with my wife</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13290358719252216483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2873699527" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2873699527" />
    <a title="Don" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99062839-don"><img alt="Don" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576651519p2/99062839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2873699527?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Don" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Don" href="/user/show/99062839-don">Don</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2873699527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14043122015745611390">Being a massive fan of George RR Martin's A Song Of Ice And Fire series, I wanted to check out some of his earlier work, Fevre Dream, the title itself is impressive, and the story involved strange vampires on big steamboats back in the olden days, I had to check this out.<br/><br/>The story is about an unlikely partnership between an ambitious Steamboat Captain (Abner Marsh) and the rich, charming Joshua York, who offers to fund Marsh's operations, Marsh wants to build the biggest, fastest Steamboat on th</span>
  <span id="freeText14043122015745611390" style="display:none">Being a massive fan of George RR Martin's A Song Of Ice And Fire series, I wanted to check out some of his earlier work, Fevre Dream, the title itself is impressive, and the story involved strange vampires on big steamboats back in the olden days, I had to check this out.<br /><br />The story is about an unlikely partnership between an ambitious Steamboat Captain (Abner Marsh) and the rich, charming Joshua York, who offers to fund Marsh's operations, Marsh wants to build the biggest, fastest Steamboat on the river, and with York planning to bankroll Marsh and build the boat, providing he accompanies him on the journey and asks him no questions about his peculiar behaviour, which does eventually attract unwarranted attention.<br /><br />As the Fevre Dream sets sail, Marsh and York strike up a mutual friendship and respect, though Marsh is understandably concerned at the strange company and strange hours York keeps and how he is never present during the daylight, Marsh makes a disturbing discovery.<br /><br />More alarming is the presence of York's old nemesis, Damon Julian, an old, ancient being who shuns York's offers and wants to stick to the old ways, aided by his odious right hand man "Sour" Billy Tipton, they seek carnage and destruction, much to York and Abner Marsh's dismay.<br /><br />This book captures the atmosphere and adventure of the steamboats sailing away into the night, from one port to another, trouble never too far away, particularly with Julian and Billy Tipton appearing on the scene, and the protagonist of the story, Abner Marsh, invokes sympathy, an ambitious and determined man, he has devoted most of his life to the river and his fellow steamboatmen gave his life a purpose, uncomfortable around women, as well as his own appearance (known as the ugliest man on the ship) he has shunned any forms of romance, and the thought of losing his beloved Fevre Dream at the hands of Julian and Tipton, rushes him and York into action.<br /><br />Well worth a look, a dark, gothic tale of vampires, friendships and steamboats, this is nothing like GRRM's later work (A Song Of Ice And Fire in particular) but an interesting read and take on the vampire tale.<br />3.75 Stars, recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14043122015745611390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_343245234" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343245234" />
    <a title="Vincent Ribaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10026136-vincent-ribaya"><img alt="Vincent Ribaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349370949p2/10026136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343245234?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vincent Ribaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vincent Ribaya" href="/user/show/10026136-vincent-ribaya">Vincent Ribaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553577938" href="/book/show/12894834-fevre-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10026136-vincent-ribaya?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343245234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5165063281178137856">I believe all authors have a certain piece of work that sadly doesn't get its due credit. For <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin' title='George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>George R.R. Martin</a>, that book would most probably be <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12894834.Fevre_Dream' title='Fevre Dream by George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fevre Dream</a>.<br/><br/>I personally enjoyed this novel, and though preoccupied with a Transition Camp for medical school, I managed to finish it throughout my 2-night stay at that camp. The book was quite fast-paced, and there are a few parts in the plot which I think could've been longer - but it all worked out quite nicely.<br/><br/>Many would claim <i>Fevre Dream</i> was a fe</span>
  <span id="freeText5165063281178137856" style="display:none">I believe all authors have a certain piece of work that sadly doesn't get its due credit. For <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin" title="George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R.R. Martin</a>, that book would most probably be <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12894834.Fevre_Dream" title="Fevre Dream by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">Fevre Dream</a>.<br /><br />I personally enjoyed this novel, and though preoccupied with a Transition Camp for medical school, I managed to finish it throughout my 2-night stay at that camp. The book was quite fast-paced, and there are a few parts in the plot which I think could've been longer - but it all worked out quite nicely.<br /><br />Many would claim <i>Fevre Dream</i> was a feeble attempt made by George R.R. Martin to reinterpret the vampire novel just as <a href="http://awoiaf.westeros.org/index.php/Children_of_the_Forest" rel="nofollow noopener">the Children of the Forest</a> was his reinterpretation of what would be <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elf" rel="nofollow noopener">Elves</a>, or just as <a href="http://awoiaf.westeros.org/index.php/Others" rel="nofollow noopener">the Others</a> was a reinterpretation of what would be frost/ice <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidhe" rel="nofollow noopener">Sidhe</a> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9814682.A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="A Song of Ice and Fire by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Song of Ice and Fire</a>. Though, just like the Children of the Forest and the Others, I personally think the master of modern fantasy - George R.R. Martin - did his reinterpretation went quite well.<br /><br />I find the book highly underrated. Many critics and reviewers gave the book relatively low ratings most probably because they were expecting something similar to <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i> - but I'd like to believe that good writers never tell two different tales in the same way (take C.S. Lewis and J.R.R. Tolkien, for example). The voice of <i>Fevre Dream</i> is definitely not that of a <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. <i>Fevre Dream</i> is told in single-setting accounts rather than in separate point-of-views like in <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>.<br /><br />Others may have disliked the book because of its theme and/or genre. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vampire" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire</a> lore is something I personally like, but I know that the it's been "done to death" by movies and perhaps even "spoiled to the core" by books and reinterpretations like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>. But that's what makes George R.R. Martin a genius in his work - he takes something that was once enjoyed by readers but has been recently "done to death" and repackages it in a way readers can once again enjoy them. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dragon" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knight" rel="nofollow noopener">knights</a>, and mysterious alien fauna have been mined to depletion by every high fantasy and science fiction book, movie, and game out there, but you see them repackaged nicely in works like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13501.The_Hedge_Knight__Graphic_Novel_" title="The Hedge Knight (Graphic Novel) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hedge Knight</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/769902.Sandkings" title="Sandkings by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">Sandkings</a>.<br /><br />Though genre and voice may seem un-Martin-like to those used to the high fantasy setting of Westeros, the tone is, in fact, very, very George R.R. Martin. I see no reason why <i>Fevre Dream</i> should be like <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>, and within the context of taking it as a book on its own, I see no problem with it being a vampire novel - just don't recall any <i>Twilight Saga</i> events and see it as a reinterpretation of vampires like Dracula or Nosferatu. Subtract the factors of it being "unfamiliar" or of it being "vampire", then you got yourself a really, really good book.<br /><br />The book follows the tale of Abner Marsh, a struggling riverboat captain who has just taken in the mysterious and odd, but wealthy, Joshua York as a new business partner. Though York's offer of a cash and a new boat, the Fevre Dream, was one Captain Marsh just couldn't refuse, it doesn't take long 'til the seasoned captain realizes that the Dream he has just gotten himself into would turn into a quite adventurous yet fantastic nightmare.<br /><br />George R.R. Martin fan, or not... Vampire fan, or not... <i>Fevre Dream</i> is a delightful read. In terms of genre, it's both quite unique, yet very familiar - probably a must-have in your personal library if you're into collecting modern fantasy novels, novels with historical fiction settings, or novels about paranormal creatures.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5165063281178137856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1955519896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1955519896" />
    <a title="Karl Marberger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58621278-karl-marberger"><img alt="Karl Marberger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593713350p2/58621278.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1662938300" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662938300" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8575414-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441431450p2/8575414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1662938300?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662938300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10510125567419464595">I have read very few vampire books and this one sets a very high bar. Set by the Mississippi in the 1850s this is story telling at its best. Martin evokes perfectly the era of the steamboat with New Orleans as a melting pot of hard living characters, slaves, freed slaves, pilots and steamboat captains, plantation overseers, Creoles. I found it clever the way Martin uses his context to highlight the parallels between the slave owners and the vampires with their 'cattle'.<br/>I loved Abner Marsh, to my</span>
  <span id="freeText10510125567419464595" style="display:none">I have read very few vampire books and this one sets a very high bar. Set by the Mississippi in the 1850s this is story telling at its best. Martin evokes perfectly the era of the steamboat with New Orleans as a melting pot of hard living characters, slaves, freed slaves, pilots and steamboat captains, plantation overseers, Creoles. I found it clever the way Martin uses his context to highlight the parallels between the slave owners and the vampires with their 'cattle'.<br />I loved Abner Marsh, to my mind the hero of this tale, with his honesty, stubborn loyalty, pride and courage. Is there hope? Can good triumph over evil? Was there any difference between the white man's dominion over slaves any the vampires' dominion over their thralls?<br />This is a must read for fans of vampire literature and even if you're not, actually. It's also nice to be able to confirm for myself that George R Martin has more to him than The Game of Thrones and he is in fact adept at a shorter and stand alone story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10510125567419464595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1656188231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1656188231" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1656188231?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780385362788" href="/book/show/17972165-fevre-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1656188231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11792461850194425960">If anyone had told me a book that was a mix between Mark Twain's tales of the Mississippi and <b>Interview With a Vampire</b> would be a good idea and enjoyable read, I would have thought them mad. But sure enough, GRRM has done a marvellous job!<br/>I knew the author had been writing for a long time before he published the first book of the ASOIAF series and for a long time I wanted to know if his other stories were equally vivid and enthralling. That combined with my love for vampires let me pick this up.</span>
  <span id="freeText11792461850194425960" style="display:none">If anyone had told me a book that was a mix between Mark Twain's tales of the Mississippi and <b>Interview With a Vampire</b> would be a good idea and enjoyable read, I would have thought them mad. But sure enough, GRRM has done a marvellous job!<br>I knew the author had been writing for a long time before he published the first book of the ASOIAF series and for a long time I wanted to know if his other stories were equally vivid and enthralling. That combined with my love for vampires let me pick this up.<br><br>At first I was a bit alienated by the Scottish narrator since this is a story about the American South and steam boats so it didn't fit the setting, but quite quickly I came to appreciate the narrator. He's really good and his native accent is a nice contrast to the southern accent he uses for the dialogues.<br><br>The story itself is about a down-on-his-luck steam boat captain who gets the offer of his life by a strange man. Naturally, he takes it, thinking they would go and live an adventurous life ... but he's in for one hell of a surprise and a very long journey.<br>It is also a story about vampires. Actually, it was quite interesting how the author portrayed that race. Especially the notion of them <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[believing in a sort of Messiah while simultaneously laughing about religious humans <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was very entertaining.<br>But that is by far not all this is about. Basically, GRRM gives us a thorough character study - what drives people, what tempts them, what corrupts them and what makes them redeem themselves. All that wrapped up in an atmospheric tale of the American South before and after the Civil War when the river was wild and so were the people travelling up and down it.<br>What really got on my nerves however, was Joshua York, the man who had paid for one of the grandest steam boats on the river, who turned out to be <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a vampire <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and his awful preaching about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[not killing anyone, not even the most vile of creatures in the story <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>! If it wasn't for him and his weak character, a lot could have been prevented easily.<br><br>The descritptions of the boats, the food, the people, the landscapes ... all is very vivid and real and atmospheric and conjures up a wonderful world, long gone thanks to a terrible war and progress. It envokes all the smells and excitement of the time. Naturally, there are dark descriptions of slavery and white trash and awful things happening to good people too. But that only serves to make the tale even darker, letting a slow sense of terror creep up ones spine.<br><br>Really nice was to see time pass. The history of the area and how it was interwoven with the story. Of course, that always brought a characteristic melancholy, a sense of loss, darkness and loneliness. However, that had another effect: the author never makes anything easy. Sometimes it was extremely tantalizing, but then I realized how disappointed I would have been had the conclusion come easier (since it would have been unrealistic, after all <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Julian is thousands of years old <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<br><br>Last but not least, the poetry by Lord Byron and Shelley was a very nice touch and I ended up googling a number of those poems because they are really beautiful.<br><br>All in all, a great story with a few weaknesses (thus not as good as ASOIAF) but I'm very glad I haven't missed out on this wild ride.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465685884i/19389383._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11792461850194425960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1543980601" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543980601" />
    <a title="Paul E. Morph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44824883-paul-e-morph"><img alt="Paul E. Morph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602970987p2/44824883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1543980601?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul E. Morph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul E. Morph" href="/user/show/44824883-paul-e-morph">Paul E. Morph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553577938" href="/book/show/12894834-fevre-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44824883-paul-e-morph?shelf=books-read-in-2016">books-read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543980601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8431040028366291516">This was my first George RR Martin book. I watch the <i>Game of Thrones</i> tv show, which is what sparked my interest in reading something by him, but thought I'd try out a stand-alone novel before I plunged headlong into <i>A Song of Fire and Ice</i>.<br/><br/>So, what did I think? Well, my initial reaction was that it was a complete swipe of Anne Rice's <i>Interview With the Vampire</i>, to be honest. As the book went on, and as Martin started to demonstrate a large Mark Twain influence as well, it started to veer away fro</span>
  <span id="freeText8431040028366291516" style="display:none">This was my first George RR Martin book. I watch the <i>Game of Thrones</i> tv show, which is what sparked my interest in reading something by him, but thought I'd try out a stand-alone novel before I plunged headlong into <i>A Song of Fire and Ice</i>.<br /><br />So, what did I think? Well, my initial reaction was that it was a complete swipe of Anne Rice's <i>Interview With the Vampire</i>, to be honest. As the book went on, and as Martin started to demonstrate a large Mark Twain influence as well, it started to veer away from being a complete swipe and go off in its own direction.<br /><br />Despite my early reservations, I found myself swept up in the tale Martin was spinning and enjoying the (steamboat) ride quite a bit. It was certainly sinister and bloodthirsty enough to satisfy the horror fan in me. I really liked the protagonist; Abner Marsh is about as unlikely a hero as you'll find in modern fiction and that accounts for a good portion of his charm. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[If he hadn't died at the end of the book, I'd have definitely liked to read more of his (mis)adventures. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Martin certainly knows how to pace a story and his prose style is delightful; I'll definitely be reading more of his work in future. As for this novel, though, despite enjoying it I felt it was too close to the 'swipe' end of the 'love-letter or swipe?' scale for me to give it more than three stars. I mean, it says on the cover that this is a groundbreaking vampire novel but his vampires, apart from <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[not being able to turn humans into vampires <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were identical to Anne Rice's. The story's even set in the same part of the world! While this wasn't enough to spoil my enjoyment completely, I'd hardly call it groundbreaking.<br /><br />Regardless of this, <i>Fevre Dream</i> remains an entertaining romp of a horror novel. You could do a lot worse.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8431040028366291516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_60475648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60475648" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1497350-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1250569584p2/1497350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60475648?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/1497350-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497350-kathryn?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497350-kathryn?shelf=gruesome-horror">gruesome-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497350-kathryn?shelf=literary-horror">literary-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497350-kathryn?shelf=favorite-covers">favorite-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60475648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16587578492869277456">Fevre Dream is an unusual novel. First, it is excellent historical fiction, set amongst the steamboats traveling up and down the Mississippi, between New Orleans and St. Louis, in the mid to late 1800's. Second, it is full of interesting characters heavily influenced and molded by their environment and professions. Second, there are vampires. A+ for the first and second. C+ for the vampires.<br/><br/>This is my first novel by George R. R. Martin. Like many readers, I am tempted to read his series A Song o</span>
  <span id="freeText16587578492869277456" style="display:none">Fevre Dream is an unusual novel. First, it is excellent historical fiction, set amongst the steamboats traveling up and down the Mississippi, between New Orleans and St. Louis, in the mid to late 1800's. Second, it is full of interesting characters heavily influenced and molded by their environment and professions. Second, there are vampires. A+ for the first and second. C+ for the vampires.<br /><br />This is my first novel by George R. R. Martin. Like many readers, I am tempted to read his series A Song of Ice and Fire but thrown off by the length, and correct me if I am wrong, that the series is still not finished. I realize Fevre Dream is solely unique from the series but all I wanted was a taste of Martin's voice. I will be reading A Game of Thrones but maybe only after I am sure the series is complete. <br /><br />Fevre Dream is a notable achievement in terms of historical accuracy, at least as far as I can tell since I was not alive in the mid 1800's and thank God for that. I need a bath more than once a month. The human characters on the steamboat, particularly Marsh, were idealistic heros and I loved every one of them for it. The descriptions of New Orleans, of the Fevre Dream, before and after certain events, and Marsh's feverish hunt towards the end were engrossing. My issues are entirely with the vampires.<br /><br />Considering the book was first published in the early 80's, I should not find such fault with the vampires, how they live, their tendencies, originations, and internal struggles. All of these things are necessary to every vampire story in varrying degress. I just did not like a single one. I did not care about their problems and would have been happy if all of the vampires were killed. No love lost here. I felt zero sympathy and wondered how anyone could. I was fine with Marsh's decisions though since his first love was his steamboat, which was very telling in my opinion. Who or what was Marsh really helping?<br /><br />The book does possess a winner of a scene, near the top of my most disliked and horrific scenes ever. It was terrible, one of those scenes many people will skim over and acknowledge as being horrific and feel great disgust towards. But if they put themselves in the scene, truly picture it, they might just become sick, which is the cause for the skimming instead of delving. It's one of those scenes which sane people find difficult to stomach. Marsh's reaction after this scene endeared him further to me. He was the epitome of an unlikely hero and perfect for the role. <br /><br />I did not care for Martin's jumps in time. The final jump made me very sad, which the author might have been going for. In the end, I am happy to have read this. Recommended for fans of historic paranormal and horrific fiction, who would choose the historic trait over the paranormal and horrific characteristics. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16587578492869277456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1377064526" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
